{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:34:56","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:34:56","title":"How Bentley has shifted gears during the pandemic","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~3/a3Bzw4QhwPg/bentley-is-redefining-luxury-for-its-100th-anniversary","description":"<p>2020 is <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/bentley-motors\" target=\"_self\">Bentley</a>’s centenary year and before pandemic planning became everyone’s focus, the company had a number of special events, launches and new models lined up. For the most part, it’s managed to keep to its schedule, even if the usual glamorous launch itineraries have been swapped out for socially distanced virtual events and car loans.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>This year also saw the retirement of Bentley’s Mulsanne model, the company’s former flagship. Cut from a different cloth than its suite of core models, the Bentley Mulsanne was a true throwback to an earlier era, hand-built on a bespoke platform and incorporating the final version of Bentley’s venerable L-Series V8 engine, originally introduced in 1959. Without the Mulsanne, and with the first all-electric Bentley coming ever closer (a date of 2025 has been suggested), the company is in a state of transformation, simultaneously trying to shape a more contemporary and sustainable definition of luxury, while taking care not to shed the sporting luxury ethos that has defined the brand for 100 years.</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287369\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/new_bentayga_-_alpine_green_-_6_0.jpg?itok=Q8aemRSF\" width=\"1460\" height=\"974\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Bentley Bentayga in Alpine Green \n</div> \n<p>This summer saw the introduction of a radically revised Bentayga, Bentley’s first foray into the SUV market. The car was originally launched in 2015 and although it has been a strong sales success, it’s never quite shaken its slightly compromised aesthetic image; the Bentayga began life as an ugly duckling. It had much in common with the original <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/porsche\" title=\"Porsche\">Porsche</a> Cayenne, in that it fell short of conveying the key characteristics of its brand, despite containing all the key ingredients.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Since the original Bentayga’s debut, Bentley has gone on to create a triumphant new version of its Continental Grand Tourer, available both in droptop and coupe form with a choice of W12 (coupe only) or V8. It also produced a new generation Flying Spur, the four-door limousine that takes the reigns from the Mulsanne as the new flagship. Both GT and Flying Spur are effortlessly elegant, exceptionally powerful automobiles that also manage to be desirable luxury objects. Can the overhauled Bentayga keep up?&nbsp;</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287370\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"2\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/bentley_continental_gt_v8_14_0.jpg?itok=LI_PZ9Df\" width=\"1460\" height=\"973\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Bentley Continental Grand Tourer \n</div> \n<p>The new car is no longer the ugly duckling of the flock. The detailing has been substantially overhauled, inside and out, with a new nose and new tailgate, both of which draw on the svelte but authoritative forms of the coupe and saloon. In total,1,000 changes differentiate the car from the 20,000 examples already sold (accounting for nearly half of all annual Bentley sales). Inside, there’s a welcome update of the touchscreen interface, bringing it more in line with the best offerings from elsewhere in the VW Group, along with digital dials, wireless phone charging, and an updated removable touchscreen for rear passengers. It goes without saying that the craft, detail and quality remain exceptionally high; this is one of the great contemporary automotive interiors. In 2+2 format (a mildly infuriating waste of space, given this car’s massive scale), every passenger is given a little kingdom of their own, a world of wood and leather.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>On the road, the V8 Bentayga embodies that most fundamental of Bentley qualities – effortless power. You sit high, simultaneously commanding over and isolated from all that surrounds you. Refinement is second-to-none, with the engine relegated to a distant hushed rumble at low speeds. Nosing the beast around tight city streets isn’t without its perils, but the cameras and sensors do a good job of guiding you away from embarrassment and eternal YouTube infamy. On highways and fast A roads, the Bentayga is just as much a competent grand tourer as any other Bentley, albeit slightly less fuel efficient (relatively speaking) and not quite as well suited to fast twists and turns. What it does best is blast its way towards the distant horizon, enveloping its occupants with an unassailable sense of power and tradition.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>The Continental GT coupe shares the Bentayga’s spirit but presents it in a different form. Both <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/cars\" title=\"Cars\">cars</a> have a mechanical complexity akin to that of the highest-end audio or mechanical wristwatch - admirable to certain quarters but baffling to the rest of us. These are truly the last of the V8s. Bentley is working furiously on every aspect of electrification, hoping that the switch from internal combustion to battery is as seamless as possible. Both GT and Bentayga have reached their apogee; it remains to be seen where next to go. §</p>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~4/a3Bzw4QhwPg\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\" />","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Thu, 13 Aug 2020 12:37:35 +0000","feedId":9788,"bgimg":"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/wp_large/s3/2020/08/bentley_continental_gt_v8_14.jpg","linkMd5":"0aca18cc1c251a7a3662dc280d31555c","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn92@2020_1/2020/08/25/00-35-15-427_465479dd1059ce1d.webp","destWidth":848,"destHeight":565,"sourceBytes":42264,"destBytes":32096,"author":"","enclosureType":"image/jpeg","enclosureUrl":"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/wp_large/s3/2020/08/bentley_continental_gt_v8_14.jpg","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/new_bentayga_-_alpine_green_-_6_0.jpg?itok=Q8aemRSF":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn42@2020_1/2020/08/25/00-35-19-242_5d1d2ebf7f3f15de.webp","https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/bentley_continental_gt_v8_14_0.jpg?itok=LI_PZ9Df":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn62@2020_5/2020/08/25/00-35-20-712_0fed9c10ee743bec.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~4/a3Bzw4QhwPg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn74@2020_1/2020/08/25/00-35-21-299_a8e43bc4f4bcf771.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598315696879},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:34:56","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:34:56","title":"Yinka Ilori’s colourful skatepark in France is a pillar of the community","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~3/LpMTI7GuWa4/yinka-ilori-colorama-skatepark","description":"<p>British-Nigerian Yinka Ilori presents the Colorama Skatepark, a new project created in Roubaix, France, as part of Lille’s World Capital of Design 2020. Sport and street art merge in this characteristically colourful space, featuring modular artworks which serve as the structure for the space.</p>\n<p>The skatepark by Ilori is part of cultural centre La Condition Publique, a creative laboratory in Roubaix merging art, urbanism and environmental sustainability. It takes over ‘Halle B’, a 1550 m² area inside a 20th century warehouse renovated by French architect Patrick Bouchain in 2004, and previously used for exhibitions and events. The institution’s brief was simple: to bring together different audiences and create a space that’s inclusive.</p>\n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\">\n<div id=\"file-287597\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\">\n<div class=\"content\">\n    <img alt=\"Yinka Ilori Skatepark Lille\" title=\"Yinka Ilori Skatepark \" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/_maxime_dufour_photographies_-13_juillet_2020_-_00321-201_0.jpeg?itok=-LKwL3tN\" width=\"1460\" height=\"973\" /></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>‘Skateboarding is a unique art form on its own,’ says Ilori. ‘It’s performative: there’s an audience, you’re doing tricks. So there is that element of display and flamboyancy - it’s quite a big thing to watch.’ The designer learned from a team of professional skateboarders, working closely with them for guidance throughout the process, which often made him reconsider his design choices.</p>\n<p>‘I think as designers, we have to understand that sometimes we’re not designing only for ourselves, but for the people,’ he says. ‘This was quite a collaborative process, which I’m really grateful for.’</p>\n<blockquote class=\"w-wide-quote\"><p>\n‘I guess the takeaway for me is, never underestimate the power of the community, and of people coming together to play.’\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Ilori’s design features different modules including ramps, partitions and blocks, and integrated the newly designed elements within the existing space through colour. The modules, as well as the structural columns and brick walls were painted in a tonal palette featuring pops of gold and fluorescent hues combined with earthy shades. The design was in part inspired by the building’s 19th century façade, characterised by lacquered tiles that Ilori recreated as a motif on the walls.</p>\n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\">\n<div id=\"file-287617\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\">\n<div class=\"content\">\n    <img alt=\"Yinka Ilori Skatepark Lille\" title=\"Yinka Ilori Skatepark \" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"2\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/_maxime_dufour_photographies_-13_juillet_2020_-_00321-155_0.jpeg?itok=0vG5Xx0M\" width=\"1460\" height=\"973\" /></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>‘I wanted to create a space that is joyful and inclusive, and that allows room for stories to be told and created. That’s why I use colour, to create memories,’ he continues. For the designer, it was important to create a space that would become a pillar of the community, a safe space for local children: ‘skateboarding is not only about skating, but it’s also about being part of a community, it’s also being part of a family,’ he says. </p>\n<p>Further cementing the skatepark’s role in Roubaix, two classes from the local high school took part in the project’s construction, and the park also offered an opportunity for youth employment, with new ad-hoc apprenticeship positions. ‘The kids came down to help us build and paint as well, it was great to get their input as well and I think there are also future designers and makers here,’ adds Ilori. ‘I guess the takeaway for me is, never underestimate the power of the community, and of people coming together to play.’ §</p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~4/LpMTI7GuWa4\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Mon, 24 Aug 2020 13:25:25 08:34:56","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:34:56","title":"The art world is rallying behind Beirut","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~3/48CO8q3_PDk/art-relief-funds-beirut-following-explosion","description":"<p>On 4 August, a colossal explosion ripped through the Lebanese capital, Beirut causing widespread destruction, mourning, anger and prompting many still-unanswered questions. Following the&nbsp;disaster, arts initiatives&nbsp;around the globe&nbsp;banded together to raise emergency funds&nbsp;for&nbsp;the&nbsp;immediate aftermath and beyond.&nbsp;Here are just a few of the&nbsp;platforms offering the Beirut people and its arts community some much-needed aid.</p> \n<h2>Art Relief for Beirut</h2> \n<p>Art Relief for Beirut was set up by Netherlands-based artist Mohamad Kanaan. Using Instagram as a call to action, Kanaan has been selling artworks and prints donated by a range of global artists. The joint 2019 Turner Prize winners, Lawrence Abu Hamdan, Helen Cammock, Oscar Murillo, and Tai Shani contributed work to the platform as a collective. Other artists who have submitted work include Aldo Álvareztostado, Cvmaea Halim, Anna Aagaard Jensen and Younès Rahmoun. In its short lifespan, the initiative has raised almost $100,000, funds directed to NGOs including&nbsp;Impact Lebanon, the Lebanese Red Cross and Baytna Baytak, a social initiative helping to locate housing for those who lost their homes in the blast. <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/artrelief4beirut/\">@artrelief4beirut</a></p> \n<blockquote class=\"instagram-media\" Mophradat</h2> \n<p>Fund the Arts in Beirut was established by Lebanese-born artist Walid Raad and is coordinated through Mophradat, a Brussels-based non-profit organisation led by Raad with a mission to create opportunities for artists from the Arab world. The art fund pledges to use donations to support the Beirut arts community impacted by the explosion in ‘transparent and flexible ways’, and will announce its methodology in the coming weeks. A statement from Mophradat on 12 August read, ‘We will direct 100% of donations to arts individuals and institutions while keeping in the spirit of our mandate, to support artists and thinkers, feminist and queer people and initiatives, and provide tools to help sustain practices rather than focus on individual projects.’&nbsp;<a href=\"http://mophradat.org/beirut-art-fund/\">mophradat.org</a></p> \n<blockquote class=\"instagram-media\" src=\"//www.instagram.com/embed.js\"></script>\n<h2>Gulf Photo Plus</h2> \n<p>Ruwa, a creative platform for visual storytellers across the Middle East; and Gulf Photo Plus, Dubai’s centre for photography have joined forces for a print sale, titled For the Love of Beirut. Within 24 hours of the blast, they had rallied over 60 artists from 30 countries – all with personal connections to the city – to share images of personal significance that had been taken in and around the Middle East. Notable contributors include Magnum photographers Newsha Tavakolian and Peter van Agtmael; Pulitzer prize winning photojournalist Michael Robinson Chávez; and Beirut photographer Myriam Boulos, whose powerful images of post-explosion Beirut capture the urgent drive for change. ‘The contributions to the sale have been hugely generous, offering their most coveted work to support the city we love,’ say organisers Tanya Habjouqa and Mohamed Somji. Available to ship worldwide, the open editions are sized 10x15”, with all proceeds (net of actual costs) going to the Lebanese Red Cross.&nbsp;Until 26 August midnight Beirut time.&nbsp;<a href=\"https://gulfphotoplus.com/fortheloveofbeirut\">gulfphotoplus.com</a>&nbsp;</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287534\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/myriam_boulos_feed.jpg?itok=vzb6yOqo\" width=\"944\" height=\"1416\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\"> \n <p>An image by Lebanese photographer Myriam Boulos, shot the day after the Beirut blast: ’Ahmad takes a break to pray in Mar Mikhael. href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CDwMxNuJoRM/?utm_source=ig_embed&amp;utm_campaign=loading\" style=\" color:#000; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; font-style:normal; font-weight:normal; line-height:17px; text-decoration:none; word-wrap:break-word;\" target=\"_blank\">Please see link in profile to purchase this print with 100% of proceeds going to support the Lebanese Red Cross. It was taken on the Corniche in Beirut in 2016, not far from the blast site. I’ve been spending a lot of time in Beirut for the last six years as a mentor in the Arab Documentary Photography Program. It has become one of my favorite cities in the world, in no small part because of the wonderful people. Please have a look at the link to see this print and many other wonderful photographs, including many by former participants in the Arab Documentary Photography Program.</a></p> \n  <p style=\" color:#c9c8cd; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px; margin-bottom:0; margin-top:8px; overflow:hidden; padding:8px 0 7px; text-align:center; text-overflow:ellipsis; white-space:nowrap;\">A post shared by <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/pvanagtmael/?utm_source=ig_embed&amp;utm_campaign=loading\" style=\" color:#c9c8cd; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; font-style:normal; font-weight:normal; line-height:17px;\" target=\"_blank\"> Peter van Agtmael</a> (@pvanagtmael) on <time datetime=\"2020-08-11T14:54:46+00:00\" style=\" font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px;\">Aug 11, 2020 at 7:54am PDT</time></p> \n </div> \n</blockquote> \n<script async=\"\" src=\"//www.instagram.com/embed.js\"></script>\n<h2>Christie’s: We Are All Beirut</h2> \n<p>Christie’s Dubai and London have announced plans for an online charity auction to support the art and cultural communities in Lebanon. Under the title, ‘We Are All Beirut’ and taking place between late October and the first half of November, the auction will include 40 - 50 lots of global and regional art, design, <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/jewellery\" title=\"Jewellery\">jewellery</a> and watches which will raise funds to rebuild Beirut’s cultural scene, including the historic Sursock Museum, which suffered extensive damage in the explosion. ‘We are committed to help and hope that many of our international clients, friends and collectors will follow our call to action.’ says Guillaume Cerutti, CEO of Christie’s. ‘Seeing the images of devastation on Tuesday 4 August will always remain in all our collective memory and our thoughts are with all families, friends and artists who have lost so much. We hope to raise enough funds with this initiative to make a significant difference.’ <a href=\"https://www.christies.com\">christies.com</a>&nbsp;§</p>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~4/48CO8q3_PDk\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\" />","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Tue, 18 Aug 2020 14:00:00 +0000","feedId":9788,"bgimg":"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/wp_large/s3/2020/08/myriam_boulos.jpg","linkMd5":"e02477bea9cac35cc226fc4f07be7e1c","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn44@2020_1/2020/08/25/00-35-14-745_f63f5873c4e5b5d4.webp","destWidth":484,"destHeight":565,"sourceBytes":54105,"destBytes":48400,"author":"","enclosureType":"image/jpeg","enclosureUrl":"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/wp_large/s3/2020/08/myriam_boulos.jpg","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/myriam_boulos_feed.jpg?itok=vzb6yOqo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn34@2020_4/2020/08/25/00-35-21-179_4ea52edebc3e00d3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~4/48CO8q3_PDk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn80@2020_3/2020/08/25/00-35-20-054_8191b967194e678f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598315696879},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 08:34:56","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:34:56","title":"Roman ruins inspire these tables from Brussels-based Cobra Studios","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~3/-MWKc7BJgtI/cobra-studios-solids-tables","description":"<p>Cobra Studios’ story begins with its founders, Kenny Decommer and Hugues Delaunay, in their need for a new dining table for their apartment. Based in Brussels and with backgrounds in architecture and fashion respectively, the pair designed and made furniture for themselves, before launching their studio and debut collection this year.</p> \n<p>While working at architecture practice Explorations Architecture, Decommer had collaborated with Dominique Perrault on new furniture for Paris’ Bibliothèque Nationale, sparking his interest in design. Delaunay studied fine art and developed his scenographic approach working as a visual merchandiser for Ralph Lauren and <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/paul-smith\" title=\"Paul Smith\">Paul Smith</a>; he currently divides his time between Paris and Brussels, working for Chloé.</p> \n<p>‘I am more technical, Hugues is more conceptual and colour-minded. We complement each other,’ says Decommer. ‘We like geometry and symmetry, but we also like asymmetry and breaking the visual balance,’ adds Delaunay.</p> \n<div class=\"image-caption\"> \n <div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n  <div id=\"file-287390\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n   <div class=\"content\"> \n    <img alt=\"White surface table tops with colourful elements\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"3\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/cobra_jeroenverrecht_5470.jpg?itok=lSDWLj0h\" width=\"1460\" height=\"2092\" />\n   </div> \n  </div> \n </div> \n <p>&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The volumes supporting the table tops emerge from the simple white surfaces </p>\n</div> \n<h2>Solids by Cobra Studios</h2> \n<p>Two years in the making, Cobra Studios’ debut collection, Solids, is inspired by Roman ruins, which the designers have studied during trips to the Italian capital, and which have fascinated Decommer since childhood. In particular, he was interested in how these ancient elements are at once disconnected from and coexist with the modern city. The new designs are based on ‘a vision of a Roman Forum’; majestic columns and walls are translated into a series of pure shapes made out of resin in bright jewel hues. These elements pierce through simple white tabletops, in tactile, sanded acrylic with a chalky finish, that appear to float.</p> \n<p>While the dining table and a low coffee table were planned from the start, the third element, a side table, was created to make use of leftover shapes. The tables’ names nod to their classical inspiration: ‘Cicero’ (the dining table), ‘Santa Maria dei Clarici’ (the coffee table), and ‘Priape’ (the side table). Completing the collection is the ‘Otho’ lamp, with steel tubes and textured glass, that references postmodern forms.</p> \n<h2>Design process</h2> \n<p>Throughout the design process, Decommer and Delaunay experimented with materials and played with found objects. For production, they worked with friends and people in their local creative community, learning along the way. ‘We want to create our own identity and our own entity,’ says Decommer, adding that they want to continue combining design and production, overseeing every element themselves, keeping things at a manageable scale. But they recognise the opportunities that come from sharing ideas and being open.</p> \n<div class=\"image-caption\"> \n <div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n  <div id=\"file-287392\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n   <div class=\"content\"> \n    <img alt=\"Tables from Cobra Studios\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"5\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/cobra_jeroenverrecht_5377_0.jpg?itok=KLOqjkEu\" width=\"1460\" height=\"2093\" />\n   </div> \n  </div> \n </div> \n <p>&nbsp;</p> \n <p>The Cicero dining table is created as a combination of geometric volumes, with a contrast between the silky grey top and legs in various bright shades </p>\n</div> \n<h2>Brussels</h2> \n<p>Their home city is an important influence on their work. ‘When we arrived in Brussels six years ago there was an underground design scene, but now you have the impression that the city and the authorities are pushing that forward to create a vibrant place,’ says Decommer, referencing projects such as the Kanal Centre Pompidou, which opened in 2018.</p> \n<p>‘The city is generating excitement about where it can go and what could happen in the next few years; everybody’s going with that flow. It’s eclectic.’ The duo’s predominantly Turkish neighbourhood has also been an inspiration, and they are currently looking at earthy materials, such as terracotta and stone, and working on a collection that will incorporate more varied visual elements.</p> \n<p>Other upcoming projects include private commissions, as well as a collection of seating (‘We need chairs, so let’s just design them ourselves and try to have fun in the process,’ they say), and designs inspired by architectural elements such as arches (they have been looking at Rome’s Palazzo della Civiltà Italiana). The pair are also exploring reusing and recycling materials and objects, including their left-over resin stock, to create new pieces. The Solids collection is a firm start from a studio full of promise. §</p>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~4/-MWKc7BJgtI\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\" and stainless steel in our designs; these raw, sturdy, functional materials are most often used in buildings, spacecrafts and tech products,’ says Vera Henco, founder and head of the brand. ‘Yet when treated right, they can suddenly be turned into super sleek, dainty pieces of jewelry. That fascinated us.’</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-286618\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img alt=\"Nyyukin cuff\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/nyukkin-2.jpg?itok=ZsAw0Dv0\" width=\"1200\" height=\"1400\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<p>The results, unlike previous pieces in past collections, eschew traditional polishing techniques and instead embrace a coarser aesthetic. Using 3D-software we develop carefully designed objects whose surfaces and curves quote the canon of forms of modern architecture,’ says Johannes Hundt, founder and head of <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/product-design\" title=\"Product design\">product design</a>. housing design that better reflects the ethnic diversity of its community, Brick By Brick, a development company established by Croydon Council in London, has collaborated with the Stephen Lawrence Charitable Trust to launch a design competition. The initiative has attracted some of London’s brightest talents to submit thought-provoking ideas that address health, sustainability and the environment.</p>\n<p>The shortlist, featuring all BAME-led practices, has just been announced, and the final winner of the competition will be commissioned to design one of Brick by Brick’s small site projects, due to start in the autumn. As well as a search for a bold new idea, the competition has been an important way for Brick By Brick to meet new architects with ethnically-diverse workforces, better reflective of the Croydon community it works with.</p>\n<p>The six shortlisted practices each demonstrated a variety of approaches, starting points and concepts. Through their design, Architecture Doing Place, researched supply chains, economic opportunities, and social mobility that occurs during the exchange from taxpayers, councils, and their investments. Gbolade Design Studio’s community living design encourages strong, integrated and extraordinary neighbourhoods through design. Similarly prioritising outstanding quality and great design, Kristofer Adelaide Architecture was inspired by Berthold Lubetkin’s quote, ‘Nothing is too good for ordinary people’.</p>\n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\">\n<div id=\"file-287452\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\">\n<div class=\"content\">\n    <img alt=\"Nimtim design\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/nimtim_architects.jpg?itok=tyq-falw\" width=\"1460\" height=\"2065\" /></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"image-caption\">\nDesign submission by NimTim Architects\n</div>\n<p>NimTim Architects, also <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/architecture/architects-directory-2020-nimtim-uk\" target=\"_self\">selected for this year’s Wallpaper* Architects’ Directory</a>, proposed a simple question to the people of Croydon – what kind of home and neighbourhood do you want to live in? While Jas Bhalla Architects chose to explore the typology of homes above linear retail parades, common in Croydon, showing how these often overlooked and undervalued places could in fact be generous and flexible places to live. McCloy + Muchemwa (supported by CZWG) used modular design and structural timber to think about sustainable building practices.</p>\n<p>Chloe Phelps, Head of design and commercial at Brick By Brick / Common Ground Architecture, said: ‘This competition has introduced us to lots of talented architects that we were not previously aware of. It has been a great opportunity to stand back and reflect on who is designing our homes and to make sure that they represent the diversity of Croydon, and to encourage other organisations to do the same. We’re really excited to see what the final six teams will produce and how their ideas can be incorporated into our development programme to bring about a permanent change.’</p>\n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\">\n<div id=\"file-287453\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\">\n<div class=\"content\">\n    <img alt=\"Jas Bhalla design\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"2\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/jas_bhalla_architects.jpg?itok=FwOeudV1\" width=\"1460\" height=\"1141\" /></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"image-caption\">\nDesign submission by Jas Bhalla Architects\n</div>\n<p>The Stephen Lawrence Charitable Trust was an ideal collaborator to help Brick By Brick reach this diverse talent. bedrooms, each with their own leafy, outdoor space – one might have a fig tree to sit under, another an pink-blossomed almond.</p> \n<p>The original bar, with its period tiled floor and industrial <a From billboards splashed across cities, to biennales devoted to up-and-comers, we tracked down the global platforms&nbsp;championing the cultural&nbsp;voices&nbsp;of the future.</p> \n<blockquote>\n <p> Tate Collective - billboards&nbsp; </p>\n</blockquote> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287477\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"5\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/responses-to-urvashi_0.jpg?itok=WRpBRPWG\" width=\"1416\" height=\"944\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Artists’ responses to \n <em>Urvashi,&nbsp;Staged Portrait, Gulmohar Park, Delhi&nbsp;</em>by Sheba Chhachhi at Seven Sisters.\n <em> Image courtesy Tate and Jack Arts</em> \n</div> \n<p>Following a Tate Collective open call, billboards across London have been filled with the work of young creatives. Members from the Tate Collective scheme, which is open to 16-25-year-olds, were invited to submit works in response to seven artworks in the Tate collection including Sheba Chhachhi Urvashi’s<em> Staged Portrait, Gulmohar Park, Delhi</em>, John Everett Millais’s <em>Ophelia</em>&nbsp;and Guerrilla Girls’ <em>Dearest Art Collector</em>. Thanks to space offered up by street advertising agency Jack Arts, the selected entries are on view until 23 August across the capital next to the work from Tate’s collection that inspired them. Following 800 submissions, from poetry to <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/illustration\" title=\"Illustration\">illustration</a> and even make-up looks, 48 works were selected, and each artist paid for their work. Maria Balshaw, director of Tate, said, ‘It is heartening to see immense creativity emerge at such a time of uncertainty for so many. Tate Collective members have engaged with Tate’s collection in ways that are truly inspiring. I hope people all over the city are delighted and surprised by the new work they find in their communities.’&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.tate.org.uk\">tate.org.uk</a>; <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/tatecollective/?hl=en\">@tatecollective</a></p> \n<blockquote>\n <p> VII Moscow International Biennale for Young Art </p>\n</blockquote> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287476\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"4\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/alisa-omelianceva_0.jpg?itok=0pkkkbjx\" width=\"1331\" height=\"944\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Alisa Omelianceva,&nbsp;\n <em>Screen Settings</em>, 2020. Site-specific installation for the interior facade of the Museum of Moscow. \n <em>Image courtesy of&nbsp;the artist</em> \n</div> \n<p>Launching on 5 September, the Moscow Biennale for Young Art will kick off with artists creating site-specific works for the interior facades of the Museum of Moscow. Following an open call which resulted in 370 applicants from 64 countries, an expert panel whittled the selection down to four projects by artists Alisa Omelianceva, Igor Samolet, Roma Bogdanov and Alina Glazoun. As a result of Covid-19 restrictions, the original biennale, which was due to begin in July, was rescheduled with an altered format comprising staggered events. Later components of the programme will include a partnership with the Cosmoscow International Contemporary Art Fair and a portfolio review programme which aims to spotlight young artists from different regions of Russia. ‘At its core, the Biennale for Young Art is not a project or an exhibition but a process, a range of tools that help us create and maintain the living environment for emerging art.’ says Alexey Novoselov, commissioner of the&nbsp;VII Moscow International Biennale for Young Art.&nbsp;<a href=\"http://youngart.ru/en/about-en/\">youngart.ru</a>; <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/young_biennale/?hl=en\">@young_biennale</a></p> \n<blockquote>\n <p> ‘Embark III’ - Gallery Ark&nbsp; </p>\n</blockquote> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287475\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"3\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/mausham-manglla-ark_02_0.jpg?itok=0EAJ-uJA\" width=\"944\" height=\"1331\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Mausham Raj Manglla,&nbsp;\n <em>Untitled 17</em>,&nbsp;2019.&nbsp;Watercolor and ink on paper. \n <em>Courtesy of the Artist, and Gallery Ark</em> \n</div> \n<p>For the last three years, Gallery Ark, based in Vadodara, India has teamed up with the University of Baroda’s Faculty of Fine Arts for ‘Embark’, an exhibition supporting young artists one year after completing their master’s courses. This year, in the midst of Covid-19, conditions were a little different. Adamant that the show must go on, the gallery adopted for a pared-back approach, moving from a physical exhibition to the digital realm. For ‘Embark III’, eight artists were shortlisted including Mausham Raj Manglla who is exhibiting vivid watercolour portraits and Kavya Kumar Bhatt, whose intricate and surreal ink compositions use the stippling technique to create an air of visual deception. As part of its push to celebrate young art, Gallery Ark has forgone its commission, with artists receiving 100 per cent revenue from sales of their work. ‘As a part of the contemporary art ecosystem, we felt it was important to create a platform to support promising talent at this critical point in their careers,’ says gallery director, Nupur Dalmia. ‘This year, the logistics of selection and display were much trickier, but we are delighted to finally have been able to pull off the exhibition in its digital iteration.’&nbsp;<a href=\"https://theark.in\">theark.in</a>; <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/gallery_ark/?hl=en\">@gallery_ark</a></p> \n<blockquote>\n <p> The New Artist </p>\n</blockquote> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287474\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"2\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/anusheh-zia-ravine-2020_0.jpg?itok=x1Er46IX\" width=\"1416\" height=\"944\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Anusheh Zia, \n <em>Ravine</em>,&nbsp;2018. \n <em>© Anusheh Zia / Image Courtesy of Anusheh Zia</em> \n</div> \n<p>An online residency programme spotlighting recent graduates from across the UK, The New Artist was launched in early August in direct response to the pandemic’s effects on emerging artists at critical points in their careers. Founder Alexandra MacKay sought to carve a space for young artists at a time of turbulence and funding cuts across the arts. Every ten days, a new artist is given an online residency as part of a curated programme offering a diverse mix of artists and media. Forthcoming residencies include work by Isobel Hill, who captures everyday chance events and explores grief as a vehicle for nostalgia, interdisciplinary Brazillian artist, Enorê who uses image-capturing technologies as stand-ins for the naked eye, and Anusheh Zia, whose multi-disciplinary practice explores spirituality and Islamic faith.&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.thenewartist.co.uk\">thenewartist.co.uk</a>; <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/_the_new_artist/?hl=en\">@_the_new_artist</a></p> \n<blockquote>\n <p> <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/hauser-wirth\" title=\"Hauser &amp; Wirth\">Hauser &amp; Wirth</a> -&nbsp;‘In Real Life’&nbsp; </p>\n</blockquote> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287473\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/dsc_0029_2.jpg?itok=N-VrbERu\" width=\"1410\" height=\"944\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Louise Hall, \n <em>13 Dead, Nothing Said</em>, 2020. Cyanotype African wax print fabric, Cyanotype screen-printed white cotton fabric, African wax print, fabric, cotton thread.&nbsp;\n <em>©&nbsp;the artist.&nbsp;Courtesy of the artist and <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/hauser-wirth\" title=\"Hauser &amp; Wirth\">Hauser &amp; Wirth</a></em> \n</div> \n<p>In response to a remarkable year for university graduates, with degree shows being cancelled or postponed across the globe, <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/hauser-wirth\" title=\"Hauser &amp; Wirth\">Hauser &amp; Wirth</a> launched a four-month international programme dedicated to the work of recent graduates. The inaugural exhibition of ‘In Real Life’ took place at <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/hauser-wirth\" title=\"Hauser &amp; Wirth\">Hauser &amp; Wirth</a> Somerset’s artist residency studios from 29 July - 2 August and featured work from ten BA(Hons) graduates from four regional universities including Bath Spa University and Arts University Bournemouth. Works included Melody Addo’s <em>Chocolate Pudding</em> and Louise Hall’s <em>13 Dead, Nothing Said</em>. This Autumn, the exhibition will move to the gallery’s LA location, to spotlight work from Cal State’s MFA programme. The project forms part of the gallery’s #artforbetter initiative, which plans to expand on its educational partnerships and stage graduate exhibitions in further locations.&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.hauserwirth.com\">hauserwirth.com</a>; <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/hauserwirth/?hl=en\">@hauserwirth</a></p> \n<blockquote>\n <p> Galerie Thaddaeus Ropac &amp;&nbsp;Jeune Création </p>\n</blockquote> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287681\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img alt=\"Galerie Thaddaeus Ropac Paris Pantin gallery\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"6\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/unnamed-1_0.jpg?itok=uI45jzaA\" width=\"1416\" height=\"944\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Galerie Thaddaeus Ropac’s 2,000 sq m Paris Pantin space.\n <em>&nbsp;Courtesy Galerie Thaddaeus Ropac.&nbsp;Photography: Philippe Servent.&nbsp;</em> \n</div> \n<p>This September, Galerie Thaddaeus Ropac will offer up its sales infrastructure and its largest Paris space to stage an exhibition of 60 young regional artists and galleries. The artists were selected by the committee of Jeune Création, an emerging artists association founded in 1949. All sales revenue from the show will be given directly to the galleries and artists involved. Taking place inside the gallery’s sprawling 2,000 sq m exhibition space, Paris Pantin from 12-26 September, the show will also involve a diverse programme of photography, performance and video. ‘This is an unprecedented time for so many, but within our art world community it is particularly challenging for the next generation of artists and young galleries’, explained Thaddaeus Ropac. ‘By offering our largest gallery space and our full infrastructure to present work by 60 young artists we can support those in our community who are most in need.’&nbsp;<a href=\"https://ropac.net\">ropac.net</a>;&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.jeunecreation.org\">jeunecreation.org</a></p> \n<blockquote>\n <p> Tong Art Advisory -&nbsp;‘Open Air’ &nbsp; </p>\n</blockquote> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287682\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"7\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/nevine_mahmoud_1.jpg?itok=sX6cZ60J\" width=\"1460\" height=\"2047\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Nevine Mahmoud,&nbsp;\n <em>Toy/Offender</em>, 2020.&nbsp;Hand-blown glass, polyester resin.&nbsp;Courtesy of Soft Opening \n</div> \n<p>On 22 August, a three-week group show will be hosted in a somewhat distinctive&nbsp;location, an open-air garage space in East Hampton. Aptly titled, ‘Open Air’, the exhibition, which will comprise mostly new work, is organised by Tong Art Advisory, a Beijing, New York and Paris-based firm representing mid-career and emerging artists with a key aim to support young talent through the pandemic. Works will be hung in a salon-style format, allowing for social distancing and ten per cent of sales will be donated to each artists’ charity of choice. Among the 15 international artists are Nevine Mahmoud, Oscar yi Hou, Caitlin Keough and American artist Alexandra Noel, who will donate her ten per cent to BEAM (Black Emotional and Mental Health Collective).<a href=\"https://www.tongartadvisory.com\"> tongartadvisory.com</a>;&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/tongartadvisory/?hl=en\">@tongartadvisory</a></p> \n<blockquote>\n <p> Edoardo Monti &amp; AucArt -&nbsp;‘(Very) Young Italians’ </p>\n</blockquote> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287702\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"8\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/lux.jpg?itok=JRCYgxvm\" width=\"1284\" height=\"944\" alt=\"\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Samuel Rosi, \n <em>Lux Omnia Vincit</em>, spraypaint on canvas.&nbsp; \n</div> \n<p>For Italian collector turned curator Edoardo Monti, investing in and fostering emerging artistic talent is a&nbsp;priority. ‘Now more than ever, we have to focus on supporting the youngest, most fragile artists’, he told AucArt, where he is currently curating an online residency programme dedicated to young art. ‘As a proud Italian, yet a citizen of the world, it is my duty to dedicate my first online curatorial project to my compatriots.’ The group show, titled ‘(Very) Young Italians’ features work by 20 contemporary Italian artists working in&nbsp;a range of media,&nbsp;and will be online until April 2021.&nbsp;And Monti isn’t stopping there. In October, he is curating the Palazzo Monti degree show, which&nbsp;showcases&nbsp;works by 18 students from academies across Italy, followed by a show of artists (mostly under the age of 30) at Mana 08:34:56","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:34:56","title":"Is this railway arch roastery the future of London’s coffee scene?","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~3/HmLxI2E0bVI/watch-house-roastery-coffee-shop-london","description":"<p>Though the usually teeming streets around Tower Bridge are eerily quiet for a Wednesday morning, there is a small, socially-distancing crowd outside the newly opened Watch House Roastery in Bermondsey. The smell of scientifically-brewed coffee has lured them from their pandemic hideouts.</p>\n<p>The space, tucked into one of the railway arches on Maltby Street, is welcoming; despite the urge of this writer to shy away from all forms of non-essential human contact, until the end of time. But Watch House’s well-crafted coffee might just tip into the bucket of essentialism. Head of Coffee Ryan Garrick, a self-styled brew nerd, is enthusiastic and knowledgeable; weighing his beans on scales to the milligram, while describing their origin down to the street name.</p>\n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\">\n<div id=\"file-287450\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\">\n<div class=\"content\">\n    <img class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"2\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/imgl5560.jpg?itok=M8X-J0lB\" width=\"1460\" height=\"1825\" alt=\"\" /></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>He talks about coffee like a sommelier talks about wine; noting the ‘balance of craftmanship and controlled precision’ required to make a truly great cup. He’s convinced there’s a market for exceptional coffee in the UK – think: £14 for a flat white – in the same way as very special wines. Although the price points remain closer to earth for the time being, Garrick (who qualified along with his Watch House team to the World Barrista Championship in Melbourne this year, since postponed by the pandemic) thinks the Maltby Street Roastery is the perfect playground in which to develop these ideas.</p>\n<p>After months of rigorous tasting trials, five beans (split into three ‘moods’ – Rituals, Ventures and Rarities) are available. The Businde variety from the Rarities collection is of particular note. ‘Coffee blossom, strawberry jam, Assam teaI,’ read the tasting notes. To this untrained palate, it simply tastes really good. ‘The average customer might not tell the difference in the same was as a coffee expert might,’ says Garrick. ‘But it’s about the pursuit of better.’</p>\n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\">\n<div id=\"file-287449\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\">\n<div class=\"content\">\n    <img alt=\"Coffee product from Watch House Roastery in London\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/embed_watch-house-businde.jpg?itok=OiOeOzWq\" width=\"887\" height=\"940\" /></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The space – which is one part coffee shop three parts experimental laboratory – was designed by London-based architecture and design studio (and Square Mile Coffee veterans) Kirkwood McCarthy. A U-shaped bar made from the same terracotta bricks that scale the walls is an impressive focal point of the arched building, which used to house Monmouth Coffee. Floor-to-ceiling windows offer views of the roaster and training room, giving visitors behind-the-scenes access to the Modern Coffee experience. At the back, a quiet ‘cupping room’ is the training ground for Watch House baristas and will be open for customer tastings and workshops as lockdowns ease. The darkened space (a cooling respite from this summer’s awkward heat) is separated from the factory floor by wooden sliding doors to create a fully immersive, and safe, experience.</p>\n<p>While the Maltby Street flagship is new, there are four other, smaller outposts dotted across the capital; meaning you shouldn’t have to travel too far to curb your Watch House craving. If you’d prefer to not leave your house at all, a recently launched subscription coffee service has you covered. §</p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~4/HmLxI2E0bVI\" Khachatryan","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~3/ff51rducqek/studio-khachatryan-st-vincent-antwerp","description":"<p>Multidisciplinary <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/antwerp\" target=\"_blank\">Antwerp</a> space St Vincent presents a summer exhibition of works by Studio Khachatryan, with a range of works including <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/lighting\" title=\"Lighting\">lighting</a>, furniture and objects.</p> \n<p>Founded by Armenian, Belgium-based Noro Khachatryan in 2010, the studio operates with a multidisciplinary approach, touching upon product and <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/furniture-design\" title=\"Furniture design\">furniture design</a> as well as architecture and <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/sculpture\" title=\"Sculpture\">sculpture</a> with a distinctively sleek aesthetic, attention to craftsmanship techniques and natural materials. The exhibition will show limited edition pieces designed between 2016 and 2020, exploring Khachatryan’s mathematical approach to design and the pure visual language of his works.</p> \n<p>All pieces in the exhibition can be traced back to a minimal, archetypal design language, stemming from a varied pool of visual inspirations. The <em>Meronyms</em>, for example, are a series of abstract objects whose volumes reference classical urban architecture. ‘The structures in this series reflect the relationship between interior and exterior within the city’s public spaces, and the way this relationship is often translated by materials,’ says Khachatryan. Made of black Noir de Mazy <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/marble\" target=\"_blank\">marble</a>, the pieces eschew traditional functions, being defined solely by their structural inspiration – platform, corner and column – thus leaving the user to approach them functionally as they please.</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287415\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img alt=\"Meronyms by Studio Khachatryan\" title=\"Meronyms by Studio Khachatryan\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"2\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/meronyms_corner.jpg?itok=kG08l74f\" width=\"1460\" height=\"1095\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  ’Corner’, from the \n <em>Meronyms</em> collection \n</div> \n<p>Other pieces in the show include the <em>Jag</em> bronze candle holders, the <em>If</em> side tables in marble and brass and the slim <em>Dy</em> pendant lamp. Every object by Studio Khachatryan is the result of a precise composition of geometries, and is enriched by the material palette and by the technical precision with which it is assembled.</p> \n<p>For the occasion, Khachatryan will also unveil the <em>Post</em> tables, a pair of plinth-like objects made of two intersecting white onyx volumes. Once again, the functional approach is left to the user, with shapes that can suggest a more domestic direction or become a white canvas-like display element.</p> \n<p>A self-proclaimed materialist, through this body of work Khachatryan demonstrates the potential richness of a minimalist design language, and the fine line between function&nbsp;and abstraction. §</p>\n<img ","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~3/LA4yG9yp-wo/savoury-scents-perfumer-h-transforms-scents-into-tastes","description":"<p>Cucumber, pear, and salt might sound like ingredients flavours into sensory delights well-matched to both. Out this month, Harris’ <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/fragrance\" title=\"Fragrance\">fragrance</a> brand, <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/lifestyle/perfumery-h-by-lynn-harris\" target=\"_self\">Perfumer H</a>, launches a new capsule of scents alongside corresponding pantry staples- a Salt&nbsp;perfume with matching table salt, a Pear <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/fragrance\" title=\"Fragrance\">fragrance</a> and complimentary jasmine tea, and a Cucumber&nbsp;scent that is just as piquant as its correlative pickled cucumber.&nbsp;</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287498\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img alt=\"pear perfume in orange glass bottle, cucumber perfume in green bottle, and salt perfume in blue glass bottle\" title=\"pear perfume in orange glass bottle, cucumber perfume in green bottle, and salt perfume in blue glass bottle\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/lyn_fragrences.jpg?itok=hZa4yedg\" width=\"1197\" height=\"766\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Pear, Cucumber, and Salt fragrances by Perfumer H&nbsp; \n</div> \n<p> Harris made her name in perfumery&nbsp;with the launch of her brand Miller Harris in 2000 and has&nbsp;since moved on to create&nbsp;Perfumer H. It’s&nbsp;a meticulously curated <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/fragrance\" title=\"Fragrance\">fragrance</a> line with an aesthetic that’s uniquely British- refined, minimal, and bold- think fashion’s <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/margaret-howell\" target=\"_self\">Margaret Howell</a> or the furniture of <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/design/take-a-seat-london-showroom-twentytwentyone-pays-tribute-to-robin-days-reclining-chair\" target=\"_self\">Robin Day</a> but in <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/fragrance\" title=\"Fragrance\">fragrance</a>.</p> \n<p>Harris brings that same sensibility to this new line of pantry goods, working with fine producers&nbsp;to create uncomplicated, high-quality fare that can easily transform the most simple of dishes.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287500\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img alt=\"perfumer h salt with blue label next to sage leaf and other herbs \" title=\"perfumer h salt with blue label next to sage leaf and other herbs \" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"2\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/feature_lyn_1.jpg?itok=BWC_c4gG\" width=\"650\" height=\"758\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Perfumer H salt made in collaboration with&nbsp;Epices Roellinger \n</div> \n<p>The salt of the Pantry Collection&nbsp;was made in collaboration with French specialty spice house Epices Roellinger, located in the childhood home of Michelin-star chef Olivier Roellinger. Harris, who had been cooking with Epices Roellinger salt throughout lockdown, concocted a Salt&nbsp;<a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/fragrance\" title=\"Fragrance\">fragrance</a> which she then asked the Roellinger family to translate into an edible seasoning.</p> \n<p>‘When I tasted it, I couldn’t believe how closely they got it,’ says Harris.&nbsp;The salt captures the&nbsp;rosemary and white sage of the <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/fragrance\" title=\"Fragrance\">fragrance</a> and enhances it with&nbsp;a hint of rose flavors and warm cardamom.&nbsp;</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287501\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img alt=\"perfumer h pickled cucumber on a silver plate with salmon and pickle \" title=\"perfumer h pickled cucumber on a silver plate with salmon and pickle \" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"3\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/lyn_cucumber.jpg?itok=DDK7ElX9\" width=\"1460\" height=\"1460\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Perfumer H pickled cucumber made in collaboration with&nbsp;Rosebud Preserves \n</div> \n<p>The watery scent of ‘Cucumber,’ a mixture of bergamot, watermelon, and lemon rind fused with cedarwood and sea moss, finds it’s a culinary compliment in pickles made by Rosebud Preserves. Located in a series of 19th-century barns in North Yorkshire, the preserve company transformed Harris’s scent into a range of pickled cucumbers flavoured with lemon rind and juniper berries.</p> \n<p>The final element of the pantry collection, violet leaf tea, is complemented by Perfumer H’s floral Pear&nbsp;perfume. The bergamot, mandarin and white pear scent is combined with rosewood, sugared musk with vanilla to make a <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/fragrance\" title=\"Fragrance\">fragrance</a> that is just as appetizing <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/lifestyle/picky-nicky-is-anti-plastic-and-promotes-eco-friendly-design\" target=\"_self\">Postcard Teas</a>’ jasmine blend.&nbsp;</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287502\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img alt=\"perfumer h jasmine tea on silver plate with silver tea pot\" title=\"perfumer h jasmine tea on silver plate with silver tea pot\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"4\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/lyn_tea.jpg?itok=4iF6Tsth\" width=\"1460\" height=\"1947\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Perfumer H jasmine tea made in collaboration with&nbsp;Postcard Teas \n</div> \n<p>Harris has worked with Tim d’Offay, <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/wallpaper-re-made\" target=\"_self\">Wallpaper* Handmade</a> alumnus&nbsp;and&nbsp;founder of Postcard Teas,&nbsp;for over 15 years&nbsp;and this specialty tea blends Darjeeling and a Miaoli White Tip Oolong with vibrant notes of blackcurrant, violet leaf and vanilla bourbon.</p> \n<p>As with previous Perfumer H perfumes, Cucumber, Pear, and Salt are&nbsp;available in glass bottles handblown by&nbsp;Michael Ruh and, for the first time, feature an&nbsp;asymmetrical typeface by <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/studio-frith\" target=\"_self\">Frith Kerr</a>, making the Pantry Collection a project that&nbsp;brings together the talents of culinary artisans, craftsmen, and designers for a truly multi-disciplinary lockdown collaboration. §&nbsp;</p>\n<img 08:34:56","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:34:56","title":"Industrial architecture inspires a villa renovation in the suburbs of Milan","link":"http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/Wallpaperfeed/~3/TNyun8wB3Xw/oasi-segrate-villa-house-renovation-milan-italy","description":"<p>Oasi Architects has designed an unexpected villa in Villaggio Ambrosiano of Segrate, a pleasant community in the Milanese suburbs. The house renovation has a unique new upper volume crafted in sheet metal. Its shape, which curves, shifts and folds around the lower level, has been extruded from imaginary lines extended from the urban planning regulation lines of the residential street.</p>\n<p>‘We are often inspired by industrial architecture,’ says Pietro Ferrario, principal at Oasi Architects. ‘There is something simple in its expression and clear in its execution.’</p>\n<p>There isn’t much industrial architecture in this quiet suburb, but the project required a refreshing approach. The former house on the site had been built in the 1990s and defied many of the local planning laws, leaving it essentially illegal. Working with the plot was always going to be tricky, but the client and architect worked together to make something of it. The client, a contractor who built the project himself, was aware of the legal problems associated with the house when he bought it cheap because of them. He called up Oasi Architects who gave him the confidence to take on the project.</p>\n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\">\n<div id=\"file-287287\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\">\n<div class=\"content\">\n    <img alt=\"Exterior and swimming pool\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/20200518_mg_5289_segrate_172.jpg?itok=dL34B7fm\" width=\"1460\" height=\"2190\" /></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Instead of a limitation, the architects used this as a starting point to shape the new design. Giving a new sense of character to the house, they defined the perimeter and shape of the new first floor by extruding the curves and alignments from the imaginary legal lines that the new house had to follow.</p>\n<p>When they took the design to the local administrators, they loved the project, and even encouraged them to use a unique material for the facade. The contractor chose a metal facade system that was to give the house an industrial character.</p>\n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\">\n<div id=\"file-287373\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\">\n<div class=\"content\">\n    <img alt=\"Interior\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"2\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/20200518_mg_5009_segrate_92_0.jpg?itok=921E8-Ar\" width=\"1460\" height=\"2190\" /></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>While inspired by the crude simplicity of industrial architecture, Oasi Architects start each project with the same question: How can architecture contain life?</p>\n<p>The interiors feature concrete floors at ground level and a grey stone staircase, however wood brings a lot of warmth. The window frames are made in pine wood the upper floors are oak. Ferrario’s favourite moment of the house is the veranda space overlooking the pool – where the family can drink a glass of wine, while the partner prepares some lunch. §</p><img
