Strong, light, economical, hypo-allergenic and non-magnetic, it was perfect for pilots, engineers and the military, but not a luxury material, not something to create dreams from. That is, until the 1970s, when watch designer and goldsmith Gérald Genta had a different vision. His early 1970s modernist steel watch designs, including the ‘Royal Oak’ for Audemars Piguet and the ‘Nautilus’ for Patek Philippe, integrated case and bracelet in a single fluid loop. His use of handbrushed and polished metalwork, typical jeweller techniques, created a new kind of luxury sports watch.</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287260\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img alt=\"Patek Philippe watch\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"1\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/steel-2.jpg?itok=7j-BJYgC\" width=\"1200\" height=\"1400\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  ‘Nautilus’ ladies’ automatic watch in steel and diamonds,&nbsp;by Patek Philippe. \n <em>Fashion: Aylin Bayhan</em> \n</div> \n<p>It wasn’t long before women’s watches were just as vigorously proportioned – the new Patek Philippe ladies’ automatic ‘Nautilus’, which eschews the smaller delicacy of earlier models with its most generous dimensions yet, is a case in point. A dark grey opaline dial, when framed by a diamond bezel, becomes almost dainty. The grey steel hue of <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/bulgari\" title=\"Bulgari\">Bulgari</a>’s ‘Octo Roma’ is made richer with rose-gold accents. Chopard’s ‘Alpine Eagle’, meanwhile, although crafted with heavy steel links, boasts a sleek, narrow silhouette, bestowing steel with the elegantly precious credentials it so richly deserves. §</p> <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/loewe\" target=\"_self\">Loewe’s</a> new line of <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/fragrance\" target=\"_self\">home fragrances</a> is inspired by the vegetable garden at creative director <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/jonathan-anderson\" target=\"_self\">Jonathan Anderson’s</a> <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/london\" target=\"_self\">London</a> home. The collection features candles, rattan diffusers, soaps and room sprays in 11 plant-inspired scents, including tomato leaves, cypress balls, pea, coriander, and cannabis.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Since taking the helm of the Spanish house in 2013, Anderson has championed <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/design/loewe-craft-prize-2020-finalists-annouced\" target=\"_self\">modern craft</a>, and this appreciation extends to the presentation of the new line. The <a href=\"http://https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/fragrance\" target=\"_self\">home fragrances</a> are housed in handcrafted ceramic containers that evoke the elegant simplicity of Ancient Greek drinking vessels, and come in a variety of colours from striking black to powder pink. The packaging, an artwork in itself, features bold still-life photographs of plants from Franco-Swiss photographer Erwan Frotin.</p> \n<p>Below, Anderson speaks more about the inspiration behind the line and his own gardening practice.&nbsp;<em>&nbsp;</em></p> \n<div class=\"image-caption\"> \n <div alt=\"tomato scented red candle and red candelabra by Loewe\" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"4\" data-fid=\"287662\" data-media-element=\"1\" data-widget=\"mediabox\" title=\"tomato scented red candle and red candelabra by Loewe\"> \n  <div class=\"content\">\n   <img alt=\"tomato scented red candle and red candelabra by Loewe\" height=\"1747\" src=\"https://cms.wallpaper.com/s3/files/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/loewe_body1_0.jpg?itok=35bTlqQY\" title=\"tomato scented red candle and red candelabra by Loewe\" width=\"1460\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n <p>Loewe tomato scented candles and candelabra.<strong>&nbsp;</strong><em>Photography:&nbsp;Adam Barclay.</em>&nbsp;<em>Originally featured in the September 2020&nbsp;issue Wallpaper* (W*257)</em> </p>\n</div> \n<p><strong>W*: Why did now seem like the right time for Loewe to branch into home <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/fragrance\" title=\"Fragrance\">fragrance</a>?</strong></p> \n<p>JA: I already had in mind to create candles and add an <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/fragrance\" target=\"_self\">olfactory dimension</a> when I first joined Loewe. I have always found the idea of senses being used as a stimulus to healing very interesting. There’s always been this thing with nature, that we draw on what we have around us, we associate smells to different things, it’s very personal.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>How did you come up with the idea of vegetable and plant-inspired scents?</strong></p> \n<p>Smells trigger memories and for me the selection of smell is quite personal. I remember as a child we had a greenhouse and we grew vegetables in it, so there’s a few smells from the collection that remind me of being a child, others that remind me more of journey’s I’ve taken, a bit like olfactory sketches. Smells are quite grounding in a way. Part Victorian, botanical garden, part apothecary, the mix is both scientific and sentimental.</p> \n<p><strong>Can you speak more about the process of designing the <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/ceramics\" title=\"Ceramics\">ceramics</a>? How did you take the inspiration of Greek drinking vessels and transform them into objects for a modern space?</strong></p> \n<p>Tactility is key for me, as Loewe’s ongoing engagement with the art of <a href=\"http://feedproxy.google.com/tags/ceramics\" title=\"Ceramics\">ceramics</a> testifies. The ribbed terracotta pot that holds our candles is based on a 5th century BC Greek mug I bought at an auction several years ago. In the rhythmic purity of this incredibly old object, I find unquestionable modernity, and function: it offered the perfect template as a container for our candles, which come in three different sizes. A classic Louis XIV-era French ambeau informs the geometry of the other candle base: craft knows no historic border for me. Speaking of which, candles are made with wax derived purely from natural ingredients and embossed with the Loewe&nbsp;monogram and the message ‘Made in Spain’.</p> \n<div class=\"media-element-container media-wysiwyg\"> \n <div id=\"file-287631\" class=\"file file-image file-image-jpeg\"> \n  <div class=\"content\"> \n   <img alt=\"jonathan anderson black and white portrait \" title=\"jonathan anderson black and white portrait \" class=\"media-element file-wysiwyg\" data-delta=\"2\" src=\"https://cdn.wallpaper.com/main/styles/responsive_1460w_scale/s3/jwportrait_0.jpg?itok=k4bzUCwn\" width=\"1460\" height=\"1826\" />\n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<div class=\"image-caption\">\n  Loewe’s creative director Jonathan Anderson. \n <em>Photography:&nbsp;Scott Trindle</em> \n</div> \n<p><strong>During your tenure at Loewe you’ve championed the power of craft to transform spaces, and I imagine the past few months of lockdown have seen you spend more time at home than you have before. Has spending so much time in one place taught you anything more about the role craft plays in making a home?</strong></p> \n<p>When we went into lockdown, on the first two weeks I was like ‘why do I have all this stuff.’ This is the longest I’ve ever been in this house because I am usually back and forth from <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/paris\" target=\"_self\">Paris</a> so that was the first time I had solid time in the house. I went through a complete rejection for all the pieces that I collect and then I asked myself why I am into this, why do I collect these pieces, this textile or <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/painting\" target=\"_self\">painting</a> or these <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/tags/ceramics\" target=\"_self\">ceramics</a>, and it’s because of my obsession about people that make things, from start to finish. The people that make things with their hands are the people that inspire me.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>In some ways, the slow-pace and often solitary act of gardening makes it so different from fashion design, yet both are creative pursuits. Has your practice of one informed the other in any way?</strong></p> \n<p>With the garden you have to look after it and the same with <a href=\"https://www.wallpaper.com/design\" target=\"_self\">design</a>. You have to look after it.&nbsp;In gardening also there is always something that stands from it, a colour, a structure versus a non-structure. §</p>\n<img
